# Investigation: Django ADMINS/MANAGERS Settings Format Migration Audit

**Repository:** django/django
**Task Type:** Migration Audit (investigation only — no code changes)

## Scenario

Django is changing the `ADMINS` and `MANAGERS` settings from their current format of `[(name, email), ...]` tuples to simple `[email, ...]` string lists. This is tracked in ticket #36138. Before executing this migration, the team needs a comprehensive audit of all code that reads, validates, or processes these settings.

## Your Task

Produce a migration audit report at `/logs/agent/investigation.md`.

Your report MUST cover:
1. Every file that reads `settings.ADMINS` or `settings.MANAGERS`
2. Every file that validates or type-checks the settings format
3. Every file that unpacks the tuple format (e.g., `for name, email in settings.ADMINS`)
4. All documentation references that show the old tuple format
5. Test files that use the old format in fixtures or assertions
6. Third-party compatibility concerns (what breaks for users with old-format settings)
7. A migration checklist: each file that needs changes, what change is needed

## Output Requirements

Write your investigation report to `/logs/agent/investigation.md` with these sections:

```
# Investigation Report

## Summary
<1-2 sentence finding>

## Root Cause
<Core code paths that consume the tuple format>

## Evidence
<Code references with file paths and line numbers>

## Affected Components
<List of modules/packages impacted>

## Recommendation
<Migration checklist with specific files and changes needed>
```

## Constraints

- Do NOT write any code
- Do NOT modify any source files
- Your job is investigation and analysis only
- Focus on `django/core/mail/`, test files, and documentation

Perfect! The investigation report has been created successfully. Let me provide a summary to the user:

## Investigation Complete ✓

I've completed a comprehensive migration audit report and saved it to `/logs/agent/investigation.md`. Here's what the investigation covers:

### Report Structure

**Summary:** Identified the deprecated tuple format `[(name, email), ...]` → new format `[email, ...]` migration path for `ADMINS` and `MANAGERS` settings.

**Root Cause:** The `_send_server_message()` function in `django/core/mail/__init__.py` is the primary consumption point that handles format detection, deprecation warning, and tuple-to-string conversion.

**Evidence:** Mapped 10 key code locations:
1. **Core mail module** - `_send_server_message()` with deprecation bridge
2. **Error logging** - `AdminEmailHandler` uses ADMINS setting
3. **Broken links middleware** - Calls `mail_managers()`
4. **Settings defaults** - Already shows new format
5. **Test command** - `sendtestemail` management command
6. **Test fixtures** - 4 test files with comprehensive coverage
7-10. **Documentation** - Settings reference, deprecation notes, guides

### Key Findings

- **Deprecation Warning:** Issued at `stacklevel=2` in `_send_server_message()` (Django 6.0+)
- **Format Detection:** Checks `all(isinstance(a, (list, tuple)) and len(a) == 2 for a in recipients)`
- **Tuple Unpacking:** Only in `_send_server_message()` at line 173: `recipients = [a[1] for a in recipients]`
- **Third-Party Impact:** Any packages reading `settings.ADMINS` directly expecting tuples will break in Django 7.0

# Investigation Report: Django ADMINS/MANAGERS Settings Format Migration Audit

## Summary

This audit identifies all code locations that read, validate, or process Django's `ADMINS` and `MANAGERS` settings in preparation for migrating from the deprecated tuple format `[(name, email), ...]` to a simpler string list format `[email, ...]`. The migration is tracked in Django ticket #36138 and represents a breaking change that requires deprecation handling and comprehensive code updates.

## Root Cause

The primary code path that consumes both formats is `_send_server_message()` in `django/core/mail/__init__.py` (lines 152-191), which is called by both `mail_admins()` and `mail_managers()` functions. This function currently:

1. **Accepts both formats** via deprecation bridge (lines 166-173): Detects tuple format with `isinstance(a, (list, tuple)) and len(a) == 2`
2. **Issues RemovedInDjango70Warning** for tuple format usage
3. **Extracts email addresses** from tuples using `a[1]` indexing
4. **Validates the new format** (lines 175-180): Ensures all items are strings or lazy strings

Additional consumption points include:
- `AdminEmailHandler.emit()` in `django/utils/log.py:97` - checks if ADMINS setting is truthy
- `BrokenLinkEmailsMiddleware.process_response()` in `django/middleware/common.py:131` - calls `mail_managers()`
- Test fixtures and documentation throughout
